<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Crossrail</h1>			<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
				<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>				<div id="contentSub"></div>
				<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the railway line in England that is currently under construction. For the precursor service introduced in 2015, see <a href="/wiki/TfL_Rail" title="TfL Rail">TfL Rail</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Crossrail_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Crossrail (disambiguation)">Crossrail (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>

<li>May 2018: <a href="/wiki/Paddington_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Paddington railway station">Paddington</a> to Heathrow stopping service transfers to TfL Rail</li>
<li>Autumn 2019: Elizabeth line will open in stages<sup id="cite_ref-Operator_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Operator-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>

<tr>
<td style="line-height:normal;padding:6px 5px 3px;text-align:center"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar"><span style="word-spacing:0">This diagram: </span><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Crossrail_RDT" title="Template:Crossrail RDT"><span title="View this template">view</span></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Crossrail_RDT" title="Template talk:Crossrail RDT"><span title="Discuss this template">talk</span></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Crossrail_RDT&amp;action=edit"><span title="Edit this template">edit</span></a></li></ul></div>
</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr>
</tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Crossrail</b> is a 118-kilometre (73-mile) railway line under development in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Home_counties" title="Home counties">home counties</a> of <a href="/wiki/Berkshire" title="Berkshire">Berkshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buckinghamshire" title="Buckinghamshire">Buckinghamshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Essex" title="Essex">Essex</a>, England. A large portion of the line, between <a href="/wiki/Paddington_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Paddington railway station">Paddington</a> in central London and <a href="/wiki/Abbey_Wood_railway_station" title="Abbey Wood railway station">Abbey Wood</a> in the south-east, is due to open in Autumn 2019. At the time of this opening, that new section and two other existing routes will be officially renamed the <b>Elizabeth line</b>, after Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a>. At each end of the central core, the line will divide into two branches: in the east to Abbey Wood and to <a href="/wiki/Shenfield_railway_station" title="Shenfield railway station">Shenfield</a> in Essex, and in the west to stations at <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a> and to <a href="/wiki/Reading_railway_station" title="Reading railway station">Reading</a> in Berkshire. Part of one of the eastern branches, between <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Street_station" title="Liverpool Street station">Liverpool Street</a> and Shenfield, was transferred to a precursor service called <a href="/wiki/TfL_Rail" title="TfL Rail">TfL Rail</a> in May 2015; this precursor also took control of <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Connect" title="Heathrow Connect">Heathrow Connect</a> in May 2018.
</p><p>In August 2018 the opening of the core Elizabeth line was delayed from December 2018 until Autumn 2019. Prior to this delay, the Shenfield branch was to have been connected to the core to Paddington in May 2019 and the branches west of Paddington were to be connected to the central core in December 2019, but this schedule is now unclear.
</p><p>The project was approved in 2007 and construction began in 2009 on the central section and connections to existing lines that will become part of the route.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> As of July 2018, it is 93% complete and estimated to cost £15.4 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Its main feature is 21&#160;km (13&#160;mi) of new twin tunnels below the city. These tunnels will run from Paddington to <a href="/wiki/Stratford_station" title="Stratford station">Stratford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canary_Wharf_railway_station" title="Canary Wharf railway station">Canary Wharf</a> in the east.<sup id="cite_ref-Crossrail1_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crossrail1-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> An almost entirely new line will branch from the main line at <a href="/wiki/Whitechapel_station" title="Whitechapel station">Whitechapel</a> to Canary Wharf, crossing under the <a href="/wiki/River_Thames" title="River Thames">River Thames</a>, with a new station at <a href="/wiki/Woolwich_railway_station" title="Woolwich railway station">Woolwich</a> and connecting with the <a href="/wiki/North_Kent_Line" title="North Kent Line">North Kent Line</a> at Abbey Wood.
</p><p>New nine-carriage <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_345" title="British Rail Class 345">Class 345</a> trains will run at frequencies in the central section of up to 24 trains per hour in each direction. It is expected to relieve pressure on existing east-west <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a> lines such as the <a href="/wiki/Central_line_(London_Underground)" title="Central line (London Underground)">Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/District_line" title="District line">District lines</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Jubilee_line_extension" class="mw-redirect" title="Jubilee line extension">Jubilee line extension</a> and the Heathrow branch of the <a href="/wiki/Piccadilly_line" title="Piccadilly line">Piccadilly line</a>. Crossrail will be operated by <a href="/wiki/TfL_Rail" title="TfL Rail">MTR Corporation (Crossrail) Ltd</a> as a <a href="/wiki/London_Rail" title="London Rail">London Rail</a> concession of <a href="/wiki/Transport_for_London" title="Transport for London">Transport for London</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-rg20140718_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rg20140718-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> in a similar manner to <a href="/wiki/London_Overground" title="London Overground">London Overground</a>. TfL's annual ticket revenues for the project are forecast to exceed £800&#160;million per year in 2020/21 and over £900&#160;million per year from 2022/23.<sup id="cite_ref-tflBP2017-12_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tflBP2017-12-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Crossrail_line" title="History of the Crossrail line">History of the Crossrail line</a></div>
