<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_proposals">Early proposals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early proposals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The concept of large-diameter tunnels crossing central London to connect Paddington in the west and Liverpool Street in the east was first proposed by railwayman <a href="/wiki/George_Dow" title="George Dow">George Dow</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Star_(London)" title="The Star (London)">The Star</a></i> newspaper in June 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The project that became Crossrail has origins in the 1943 <a href="/wiki/County_of_London_Plan" title="County of London Plan">County of London Plan</a> and 1944 <a href="/wiki/Greater_London_Plan" title="Greater London Plan">Greater London Plan</a> by <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Abercrombie" title="Patrick Abercrombie">Patrick Abercrombie</a>. These led to a specialist investigation by the Railway (London Plan) Committee, appointed in 1944 and reporting in 1946 and 1948.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The term "Crossrail" emerged in the 1974 London Rail Study Report.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Although the idea was seen as imaginative, only a brief estimate of cost was given: £300&#160;million. A feasibility study was recommended as a high priority so that the practicability and costs of the scheme could be determined. It was also suggested that the alignment of the tunnels should be safeguarded<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (October 2013)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> while a final decision was taken.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_proposals">Later proposals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Later proposals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Central London Rail Study of 1989 proposed tunnels linking the existing rail network as the "East–West Crossrail", "City Crossrail", and "North–South Crossrail" schemes. The east–west scheme was for a line from Liverpool Street to Paddington/Marylebone with two connections at its western end linking the tunnel to the <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Main_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Western Main Line">Great Western Main Line</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_line" title="Metropolitan line">Metropolitan line</a> on the Underground. The City route was shown as a new connection across the <a href="/wiki/City_of_London" title="City of London">City of London</a> linking the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Route" title="Great Northern Route">Great Northern Route</a> with London Bridge.
</p><p>The north–south line proposed routing <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a>, Thameslink, and Great Northern trains through Euston and <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">King's Cross</a>/<a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_railway_station" title="St Pancras railway station">St Pancras</a>, then under the <a href="/wiki/West_End_of_London" title="West End of London">West End</a> via <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Court_Road_tube_station" title="Tottenham Court Road tube station">Tottenham Court Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piccadilly_Circus_tube_station" title="Piccadilly Circus tube station">Piccadilly Circus</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_Victoria_station" title="London Victoria station">Victoria</a> towards <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_railway_station" title="Crystal Palace railway station">Crystal Palace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hounslow_railway_station" title="Hounslow railway station">Hounslow</a>. The report also recommended a number of other schemes including a "Thameslink Metro" route enhancement, and the Chelsea–Hackney line. The cost of the east–west scheme including rolling stock was estimated at £885&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1991 a <a href="/wiki/Private_bill" title="Private bill">private bill</a> was submitted to Parliament for a scheme including a new underground line from Paddington to Liverpool Street.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The bill was promoted by London Underground and British Rail, and supported by the government; it was rejected by the Private Bill Committee in 1994<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> on the grounds that a case had not been made, though the government issued "Safeguarding Directions", protecting the route from any development that would jeopardise future schemes.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2001 Cross London Rail Links (CLRL), a joint-venture between <a href="/wiki/Transport_for_London" title="Transport for London">TfL</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">DfT</a>, was formed to develop and promote the Crossrail scheme,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and also a Wimbledon–Hackney scheme.
</p><p>While CLRL was promoting the Crossrail project, alternative schemes were being proposed. In 2002 GB Railways put forward a scheme called SuperCrossRail which would link regional stations such as <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_railway_station" title="Cambridge railway station">Cambridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guildford_railway_station" title="Guildford railway station">Guildford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oxford_railway_station" title="Oxford railway station">Oxford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Central_railway_station" title="Milton Keynes Central railway station">Milton Keynes Central</a> <a href="/wiki/Southend_Victoria_railway_station" title="Southend Victoria railway station">Southend Victoria</a> and  <a href="/wiki/Ipswich_railway_station" title="Ipswich railway station">Ipswich</a> via a west-east rail tunnel through central London. The tunnel would follow an alignment along the River Thames, with stations at <a href="/wiki/Charing_Cross_railway_station" title="Charing Cross railway station">Charing Cross</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blackfriars_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Blackfriars railway station">Blackfriars</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_Bridge_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="London Bridge railway station">London Bridge</a>. In 2004 another proposal named <a href="/wiki/Superlink_(railway_network)" title="Superlink (railway network)">Superlink</a> was promoted by a group of senior railway managers. Like SuperCrossRail, Superlink envisaged linking a number of regional stations via a tunnel through London, but advocated the route already safeguarded for Crossrail. CLRL evaulated both proposals and rejected them due to concerns about network capacity and cost issues.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-rival_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-rival-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-clrl_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clrl-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Approval">Approval</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Approval">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Crossrail_Act_2008" title="Crossrail Act 2008">Crossrail Act 2008</a> was given royal assent in July 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> giving CLRL the powers necessary to build the line.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Construction began on 15 May 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In September 2009 the project received £1&#160;billion in funding. The money was lent to TfL by the <a href="/wiki/European_Investment_Bank" title="European Investment Bank">European Investment Bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Additional_funding_secured_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Additional_funding_secured-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Both the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> parties made commitments in their manifestos for the 2010 election to deliver the railway, and the coalition government formed after the election also committed to the project.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The original schedule was that the first trains would run in 2017, but in 2010 the government delayed this to 2018 in order to save £1&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction_works">Construction works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Construction works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="#Construction"> §&#160;Construction</a></div>
<p>Construction of the new Crossrail line commenced on 15 May 2009 at <a href="/wiki/Canary_Wharf_railway_station" title="Canary Wharf railway station">Canary Wharf station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-construction2009_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-construction2009-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>In August 2018, four months before the scheduled opening of the core section of the Elizabeth line, it was announced that the project would be delayed and that the line would not open until Autumn 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcnews-310818_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcnews-310818-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Route">Route</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Route">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heathrow_Airport_tube_and_rail_stations.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Heathrow_Airport_tube_and_rail_stations.png/220px-Heathrow_Airport_tube_and_rail_stations.png" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Heathrow_Airport_tube_and_rail_stations.png/330px-Heathrow_Airport_tube_and_rail_stations.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Heathrow_Airport_tube_and_rail_stations.png/440px-Heathrow_Airport_tube_and_rail_stations.png 2x" data-file-width="1058" data-file-height="1129" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heathrow_Airport_tube_and_rail_stations.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A western branch of the Elizabeth line will serve three stations at Heathrow Airport</div></div></div>
<p>Crossrail's central core section will use new east–west twin tunnels under central London, splitting into two branches at either end. The tunnelled sections will be approximately 22 kilometres (14&#160;mi) in length.
</p><p>In the east, the line splits at <a href="/wiki/Whitechapel_station" title="Whitechapel station">Whitechapel</a>, with one branch running over the existing <a href="/wiki/Great_Eastern_Main_Line" title="Great Eastern Main Line">Great Eastern Main Line</a> via <a href="/wiki/Stratford_station" title="Stratford station">Stratford</a> to <a href="/wiki/Shenfield_railway_station" title="Shenfield railway station">Shenfield</a>, and the other branch running through <a href="/wiki/Canary_Wharf_railway_station" title="Canary Wharf railway station">Canary Wharf</a> and emerging from the tunnel at <a href="/wiki/Custom_House_for_Excel_DLR_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Custom House for Excel DLR station">Custom House</a> on a disused part of the <a href="/wiki/North_London_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="North London Line">North London Line</a>, continuing under the <a href="/wiki/River_Thames" title="River Thames">River Thames</a> to <a href="/wiki/Abbey_Wood_railway_station" title="Abbey Wood railway station">Abbey Wood</a>.
</p><p>In the west the route connects with the <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Main_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Western Main Line">Great Western Main Line</a> at <a href="/wiki/Paddington_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Paddington station">Paddington</a> and runs to <a href="/wiki/Hayes_and_Harlington_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Hayes and Harlington railway station">Hayes and Harlington</a>, where it splits. One branch runs to <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Central_railway_station" title="Heathrow Central railway station">Heathrow Central</a> (for Terminals 2 and 3), <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Terminal_4_railway_station" title="Heathrow Terminal 4 railway station">Heathrow Terminal 4</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Terminal_5_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Heathrow Terminal 5 railway station">Heathrow Terminal 5</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Heathrow_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heathrow-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> while the other runs over the existing main line to <a href="/wiki/Reading_railway_station" title="Reading railway station">Reading</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Reading_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Reading-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DfT_Reading_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DfT_Reading-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Western_branches">Western branches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Western branches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paddington_-_TfL_345015_Hayes_service.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Paddington_-_TfL_345015_Hayes_service.JPG/220px-Paddington_-_TfL_345015_Hayes_service.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Paddington_-_TfL_345015_Hayes_service.JPG/330px-Paddington_-_TfL_345015_Hayes_service.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Paddington_-_TfL_345015_Hayes_service.JPG/440px-Paddington_-_TfL_345015_Hayes_service.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1366" data-file-height="910" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paddington_-_TfL_345015_Hayes_service.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Currently the western terminus, <a href="/wiki/Paddington_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Paddington station">Paddington</a> will be a major interchange for Crossrail</div></div></div>
<p>The main western section runs on the surface from Reading to <a href="/wiki/Acton_Main_Line_railway_station" title="Acton Main Line railway station">Acton Main Line</a>. Upgrades are being made to stations at <a href="/wiki/Maidenhead_railway_station" title="Maidenhead railway station">Maidenhead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taplow_railway_station" title="Taplow railway station">Taplow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burnham_railway_station" title="Burnham railway station">Burnham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slough_railway_station" title="Slough railway station">Slough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Langley_railway_station" title="Langley railway station">Langley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iver_railway_station" title="Iver railway station">Iver</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Drayton_railway_station" title="West Drayton railway station">West Drayton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hayes_%26_Harlington_railway_station" title="Hayes &amp; Harlington railway station">Hayes &amp; Harlington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southall_railway_station" title="Southall railway station">Southall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hanwell_railway_station" title="Hanwell railway station">Hanwell</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Ealing_railway_station" title="West Ealing railway station">West Ealing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ealing_Broadway_station" title="Ealing Broadway station">Ealing Broadway</a> and Acton Main Line.
</p><p>A "dive-under" was constructed at Acton to allow passenger trains to pass slower freight trains leaving and entering a goods yard. It was completed in July 2016 and was brought into use in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Heathrow spur has three stations, at Heathrow Central (for Terminals 2 and 3), Terminal 4 and Terminal 5,<sup id="cite_ref-Heathrow_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heathrow-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> and joins the main route at Airport Junction, between West Drayton and Hayes and Harlington.
</p><p>Construction of a flyover near Hayes &amp; Harlington station began in 2014, and will allow Heathrow Express trains to pass over the track used by Crossrail, avoiding delays caused by crossings.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Crossrail had been planned to terminate at Maidenhead, with an extension to Reading safeguarded.<sup id="cite_ref-safeguarding_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-safeguarding-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> On 27 March 2014, however, it was announced that the line would indeed extend to Reading.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Reading_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Reading-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DfT_Reading_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DfT_Reading-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TfL_Reading_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TfL_Reading-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_section">Central section</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Central section">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The central tunnels run from a portal just west of Paddington to Whitechapel, with further tunnelling to Stratford and to Canary Wharf.
</p><p>There will be new stations at Paddington, <a href="/wiki/Bond_Street_tube_station" title="Bond Street tube station">Bond Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Court_Road_tube_station" title="Tottenham Court Road tube station">Tottenham Court Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Farringdon_station" title="Farringdon station">Farringdon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Street_station" title="Liverpool Street station">Liverpool Street</a> and Whitechapel, with interchanges with the London Underground and other National Rail services. Due to the size and positioning of the new platforms, Farringdon station will also be connected to <a href="/wiki/Barbican_tube_station" title="Barbican tube station">Barbican</a> station, and Liverpool Street to <a href="/wiki/Moorgate_station" title="Moorgate station">Moorgate</a> station.
</p><p>Positioning a new station at Paddington presented structural design challenges due to its positioning just below Eastbourne Terrace and the station's taxi rank, and within 3&#160;m (10&#160;ft) of Isambard Kingdom Brunel's 150 year old mainline station.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_branches">Eastern branches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Eastern branches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Unit_345007_at_Liverpool_Street_7th_July_2017_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Unit_345007_at_Liverpool_Street_7th_July_2017_02.jpg/220px-Unit_345007_at_Liverpool_Street_7th_July_2017_02.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Unit_345007_at_Liverpool_Street_7th_July_2017_02.jpg/330px-Unit_345007_at_Liverpool_Street_7th_July_2017_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Unit_345007_at_Liverpool_Street_7th_July_2017_02.jpg/440px-Unit_345007_at_Liverpool_Street_7th_July_2017_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Unit_345007_at_Liverpool_Street_7th_July_2017_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Street_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Liverpool Street railway station">Liverpool Street</a> is the terminus of the eastern branches until through services start in 2019</div></div></div>
<p>One of the two eastern sections runs underground from Whitechapel to Stratford, then on the surface on the existing main line. The service will replace the "Shenfield metro", with key stops at <a href="/wiki/Ilford_railway_station" title="Ilford railway station">Ilford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romford_railway_station" title="Romford railway station">Romford</a> (for interchange with <a href="/wiki/London_Overground" title="London Overground">London Overground</a> services to <a href="/wiki/Upminster_station" title="Upminster station">Upminster</a>), <a href="/wiki/Gidea_Park_railway_station" title="Gidea Park railway station">Gidea Park</a> (where some peak hour trains will start or terminate), and Shenfield.
</p><p>The other eastern branch runs underground from Whitechapel to Canary Wharf and Abbey Wood. It takes over the Custom House to <a href="/wiki/Woolwich_railway_station" title="Woolwich railway station">Woolwich</a> via Connaught tunnel stretch of the former North London Line built by the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Counties_and_Thames_Junction_Railway" title="Eastern Counties and Thames Junction Railway">Eastern Counties and Thames Junction Railway</a>, and connects it with the <a href="/wiki/North_Kent_Line" title="North Kent Line">North Kent Line</a> via a tunnel under the Thames at <a href="/wiki/North_Woolwich" title="North Woolwich">North Woolwich</a>. It will include a <a href="/wiki/Station_box" title="Station box">station box</a> at Woolwich,<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> however, efforts to connect Crossrail with <a href="/wiki/London_City_Airport" title="London City Airport">London City Airport</a> were not fruitful.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Restoration of the Connaught tunnel by filling with concrete foam and reboring, as originally intended, was deemed too great a risk to the structural integrity of the tunnel, and so the docks above were drained to give access to the tunnel roof in order to enlarge its profile. This work took place during 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:CrossrailLine1Map.svg" class="image"><img alt="CrossrailLine1Map.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/CrossrailLine1Map.svg/800px-CrossrailLine1Map.svg.png" width="800" height="204" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/CrossrailLine1Map.svg/1200px-CrossrailLine1Map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/CrossrailLine1Map.svg/1600px-CrossrailLine1Map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1960" data-file-height="500" /></a></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Design_and_infrastructure">Design and infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Design and infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Name_and_identity">Name and identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Name and identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TFL_Rail_roundel.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/TFL_Rail_roundel.svg/220px-TFL_Rail_roundel.svg.png" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/TFL_Rail_roundel.svg/330px-TFL_Rail_roundel.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/TFL_Rail_roundel.svg/440px-TFL_Rail_roundel.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="414" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TFL_Rail_roundel.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The interim TfL Rail brand being used until Autumn 2019<sup id="cite_ref-panel_presentation022015_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-panel_presentation022015-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_line_roundel.svg" class="image"><img alt="Elizabeth line roundel" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Elizabeth_line_roundel.svg/220px-Elizabeth_line_roundel.svg.png" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Elizabeth_line_roundel.svg/330px-Elizabeth_line_roundel.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Elizabeth_line_roundel.svg/440px-Elizabeth_line_roundel.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="404" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_line_roundel.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The purple Elizabeth line roundel which will be used from Autumn 2019</div></div></div>
<p>Crossrail is the name of the construction project and of the <a href="/wiki/Limited_company" title="Limited company">limited company</a>, wholly owned by TfL, that was formed to carry out construction works.<sup id="cite_ref-crossrailltd-about_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crossrailltd-about-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since May 2015, rail services on future Crossrail route that are now managed by TfL are being operated under the temporary brand name of <a href="/wiki/TfL_Rail" title="TfL Rail">TfL Rail</a>. Trains on the Paddington–Heathrow and Liverpool Street–Shenfield routes are painted with Crossrail livery and bear the TfL Rail logo, a <a href="/wiki/London_Underground#Roundel" title="London Underground">Transport for London Roundel</a> in TfL Blue, emblazoned with the TfL Rail name in white.<sup id="cite_ref-tflrail-what_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tflrail-what-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In late 2019, when Crossrail comes into full service with an east-west service across central London, the line will be rebranded as the Elizabeth line, named after <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Standard_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Standard-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> 
Rolling stock and signage on the Elizabeth line will use a version of the Transport for London <a href="/wiki/Roundel" title="Roundel">roundel</a> that will form part of the existing branding family of <a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Transport_for_London_roundels" class="extiw" title="commons:Transport for London roundels">TfL roundel variants</a>. The Elizabeth line roundel will be coloured <a href="/wiki/Pantone" title="Pantone">Pantone</a> 266 purple crossed with a horizontal bar in TfL Blue (Pantone 072) emblazoned with the <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">elizabeth line</span> name in the corporate <a href="/wiki/Johnston_Underground" class="mw-redirect" title="Johnston Underground">Johnston Underground</a> typeface.<sup id="cite_ref-designidiom_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-designidiom-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tunnels">Tunnels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Tunnels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are five tunnelled sections, each with an internal diameter of 6.2&#160;m (20&#160;ft 4&#160;in)<sup id="cite_ref-tbm1_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tbm1-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> (compared with 3.81&#160;m (12&#160;ft 6&#160;in) for the deep-level <a href="/wiki/Victoria_line" title="Victoria line">Victoria line</a>), totalling 21&#160;km (13&#160;mi) in length: a 6.4&#160;km (4.0&#160;mi) tunnel from near <a href="/wiki/Royal_Oak_tube_station" title="Royal Oak tube station">Royal Oak Underground station</a> to <a href="/wiki/Farringdon_station" title="Farringdon station">Farringdon</a>; an 8.3&#160;km (5.2&#160;mi) tunnel from <a href="/wiki/Limmo_Peninsula" title="Limmo Peninsula">Limmo Peninsula</a> in Canning Town to Farringdon; a 2.7&#160;km (1.7&#160;mi) tunnel from <a href="/wiki/Pudding_Mill_Lane_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Pudding Mill Lane station">Pudding Mill Lane</a> near <a href="/wiki/Stratford_station" title="Stratford station">Stratford</a> to <a href="/wiki/Stepney_Green_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Stepney Green station">Stepney Green</a>; a 2.6&#160;km (1.6&#160;mi) tunnel from <a href="/wiki/Plumstead_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Plumstead station">Plumstead</a> to North Woolwich (Thames tunnel section); and a 0.9&#160;km (0.6&#160;mi) tunnel from Limmo Peninsula to the Victoria Dock portal which re-uses the Pudding Mill Lane to Stepney tunnelling machines.
</p><p>Each section consists of two tunnels excavated at the same time, with two <a href="/wiki/Tunnel_boring_machine" title="Tunnel boring machine">tunnel boring machines</a> (TBMs) per section. The tunnel linings are constructed from concrete sections, some of which are produced in <a href="/wiki/Chatham_Dockyard" title="Chatham Dockyard">Chatham Dockyard</a> then transported by barge to the Limmo Peninsula. Tunnelling is expected to progress at around 100&#160;m (330&#160;ft) per week.<sup id="cite_ref-tbm1_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tbm1-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The main tunnelling contracts are valued at around £1.5&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The wide diameter tunnels allow for new <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_345" title="British Rail Class 345">Class 345</a> rolling stock, which is larger than the traditional deep-level tube trains. The tunnels allow for the emergency evacuation of passengers through the side-doors rather than along the length of the train. When bicycles are allowed to be carried it is regarded as essential to allow evacuation to the sides of the train.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Crossrail has often been compared to Paris' <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9seau_express_r%C3%A9gional" class="mw-redirect" title="Réseau express régional">RER</a> system due to the length of the central tunnel.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stations">Stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As well as nine new stations, Crossrail requires significant work on existing station infrastructure. Although initially the trains will be 200 metres (660 feet) long, platforms at the new stations in the central core are being built to enable 240&#160;m (790&#160;ft) long trains in case of possible future extensions. At existing stations, platforms are being lengthened accordingly.<sup id="cite_ref-Dock_Mockups_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dock_Mockups-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the eastern section, <a href="/wiki/Maryland_railway_station" title="Maryland railway station">Maryland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manor_Park_railway_station" title="Manor Park railway station">Manor Park</a> will not have platform extensions, so trains will use <a href="/wiki/Selective_door_opening" class="mw-redirect" title="Selective door opening">selective door opening</a> instead.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> At Maryland this is because of the prohibitive cost of extensions and the poor business case,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> and at Manor Park it is due to the presence of a freight loop that would otherwise be cut off.<sup id="cite_ref-hol_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hol-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A mock-up of the new stations was built in Bedfordshire to ensure that the architectural integrity would last for a century.<sup id="cite_ref-Dock_Mockups_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dock_Mockups-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> It was planned to bring at least one mock-up to London for the public to view the design and give feedback before final construction commenced.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_mockup_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_mockup-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Of the 40 stations, 32 will have step-free access to both platforms;<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> train doors will be level with the platforms at central stations and at Heathrow. The stations will be fully equipped with CCTV<sup id="cite_ref-accessible_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-accessible-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (October 2013)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and, due to the length of the platforms, train indicators will be above the platform-edge doors in central stations.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_mockup_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_mockup-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It was announced on 5 July 2017 that Crossrail services would be extended to Heathrow Terminal 5 from December 2019, meaning that all Heathrow terminals will have a Crossrail service when the full service commences in December 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rolling_stock">Rolling stock</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Rolling stock">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Unit_345007_at_Shenfield_7th_July_2017_06.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Unit_345007_at_Shenfield_7th_July_2017_06.jpg/220px-Unit_345007_at_Shenfield_7th_July_2017_06.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Unit_345007_at_Shenfield_7th_July_2017_06.jpg/330px-Unit_345007_at_Shenfield_7th_July_2017_06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Unit_345007_at_Shenfield_7th_July_2017_06.jpg/440px-Unit_345007_at_Shenfield_7th_July_2017_06.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Unit_345007_at_Shenfield_7th_July_2017_06.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_345" title="British Rail Class 345">Class 345</a> train in Elizabeth Line livery, with temporary <a href="/wiki/TFL_Rail" class="mw-redirect" title="TFL Rail">TFL Rail</a> branding</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_345" title="British Rail Class 345">British Rail Class 345</a></div>
<p>Crossrail will operate new Class 345 trains.<sup id="cite_ref-Press_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Press-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The requirement is for 65 trains, each 200 metres (660 feet) long and carrying up to 1,500 passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-Press_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Press-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The trains will be accessible, including dedicated areas for wheelchairs, with audio and visual announcements, <a href="/wiki/CCTV" class="mw-redirect" title="CCTV">CCTV</a> and speaker-phones connected to the driver in case of emergency.<sup id="cite_ref-accessible_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-accessible-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Crossrail has stated that the new trains will be based on existing designs to minimise costs associated with development.<sup id="cite_ref-crprogress20100927_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crprogress20100927-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> They will run at up to 140&#160;km/h (90&#160;mph) on certain parts of the route.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2011, Crossrail announced that five bidders had been shortlisted for the contract to build the Class 345 and its associated depot.<sup id="cite_ref-rgi20110330_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rgi20110330-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> One of the bidders, <a href="/wiki/Alstom" title="Alstom">Alstom</a>, withdrew from the process in July 2011. In February 2012, Crossrail issued an <i>invitation to negotiate</i> to <a href="/wiki/Construcciones_y_Auxiliar_de_Ferrocarriles" title="Construcciones y Auxiliar de Ferrocarriles">CAF</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siemens_Mobility" title="Siemens Mobility">Siemens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hitachi" title="Hitachi">Hitachi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Transportation" title="Bombardier Transportation">Bombardier</a>, with tenders expected to be submitted by mid-2012.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, Siemens also withdrew from the bid, but will provide signalling and control systems for Crossrail.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2014, <a href="/wiki/Transport_for_London" title="Transport for London">Transport for London</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a> announced that the contract to build and maintain the new rolling stock had been awarded to Bombardier.<sup id="cite_ref-rgi20140206_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rgi20140206-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The contract covers the supply, delivery and maintenance of 65 new trains and a depot at <a href="/wiki/Old_Oak_Common_TMD" title="Old Oak Common TMD">Old Oak Common</a>. The trains are being built at Bombardier's <a href="/wiki/Derby_Litchurch_Lane_Works" title="Derby Litchurch Lane Works">Derby Litchurch Lane Works</a>. This contract will support around 760 UK manufacturing jobs plus 80 apprenticeships. An estimated 74 per cent of contract spend is expected to remain in the UK economy.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The design will be based on Bombardier's <a href="/wiki/Aventra" title="Aventra">Aventra</a> design. The first Class 345 train entered service on 22 June 2017 and they are notable in that they are the first mainline trains in Britain since 1962 to not have a yellow warning panel of any kind painted on the driving ends.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electrification_and_signalling">Electrification and signalling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Electrification and signalling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Crossrail will use <a href="/wiki/25_kV_AC" class="mw-redirect" title="25 kV AC">25 kV, 50&#160;Hz AC</a> <a href="/wiki/Overhead_lines" class="mw-redirect" title="Overhead lines">overhead lines</a>, as on the <a href="/wiki/Great_Eastern_Main_Line" title="Great Eastern Main Line">Great Eastern Main Line</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Main_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Western Main Line">Great Western Main Line</a> as far as Airport Junction. Overhead electrification has been installed between Airport Junction and <a href="/wiki/Didcot_Parkway_railway_station" title="Didcot Parkway railway station">Didcot Parkway</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/21st-century_modernisation_of_the_Great_Western_Main_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="21st-century modernisation of the Great Western Main Line">21st-century modernisation of the Great Western Main Line</a> (GWML upgrade), but Crossrail will only use it as far as <a href="/wiki/Reading_railway_station" title="Reading railway station">Reading</a>.
</p><p>The signalling will be a mixture of <a href="/wiki/European_Train_Control_System" title="European Train Control System">ETCS 2</a> on the western branches from 2019, <a href="/wiki/Communication-based_train_control" class="mw-redirect" title="Communication-based train control">communication-based train control</a> with <a href="/wiki/Automatic_train_operation" title="Automatic train operation">automatic train operation</a> on the core and Abbey Wood branch (with a possible later upgrade to ETCS), and <a href="/wiki/Automatic_Warning_System" title="Automatic Warning System">Automatic Warning System</a> with <a href="/wiki/Train_Protection_%26_Warning_System" title="Train Protection &amp; Warning System">Train Protection &amp; Warning System</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Great_Eastern_Main_Line" title="Great Eastern Main Line">Great Eastern Main Line</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-boriswatch_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boriswatch-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (October 2013)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Depots">Depots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Depots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Crossrail will have two depots, in west London at Old Oak Common and in east London at a new signalling centre at <a href="/wiki/Romford_railway_station" title="Romford railway station">Romford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">Construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Crossrail_Tunnel_Royal_Oak_Portal_Construction.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Crossrail_Tunnel_Royal_Oak_Portal_Construction.jpg/220px-Crossrail_Tunnel_Royal_Oak_Portal_Construction.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Crossrail_Tunnel_Royal_Oak_Portal_Construction.jpg/330px-Crossrail_Tunnel_Royal_Oak_Portal_Construction.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Crossrail_Tunnel_Royal_Oak_Portal_Construction.jpg/440px-Crossrail_Tunnel_Royal_Oak_Portal_Construction.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="681" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Crossrail_Tunnel_Royal_Oak_Portal_Construction.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Construction of the Crossrail portal at Royal Oak, from a footbridge to the west of <a href="/wiki/Royal_Oak_tube_station" title="Royal Oak tube station">Royal Oak Underground station</a>, July 2011</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chronology">Chronology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Chronology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Crossrail_construction_TCR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Crossrail_construction_TCR.jpg/220px-Crossrail_construction_TCR.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Crossrail_construction_TCR.jpg/330px-Crossrail_construction_TCR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Crossrail_construction_TCR.jpg/440px-Crossrail_construction_TCR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Crossrail_construction_TCR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Construction of Crossrail at Tottenham Court Road in September 2011</div></div></div>
<p>In April 2009, Crossrail announced that 17 firms had secured 'Enabling Works Framework Agreements' and would now be able to compete for packages of works.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> At the peak of construction up to 14,000 people are expected to be needed in the project's supply chain.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Work began on 15 May 2009 when <a href="/wiki/Deep_foundation" title="Deep foundation">piling</a> works started at the future <a href="/wiki/Canary_Wharf_railway_station" title="Canary Wharf railway station">Canary Wharf station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-construction2009_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-construction2009-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The threat of diseases being released by work on the project was raised by <a href="/wiki/David_James,_Baron_James_of_Blackheath" title="David James, Baron James of Blackheath">Lord James of Blackheath</a> at the passing of the Crossrail Bill. He told the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a> select committee that 682 victims of <a href="/wiki/Anthrax" title="Anthrax">anthrax</a> had been brought into <a href="/wiki/Smithfield,_London" title="Smithfield, London">Smithfield</a> in <a href="/wiki/Farringdon,_London" title="Farringdon, London">Farringdon</a> with some contaminated meat in 1520 and then buried in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> On 24 June 2009 it was reported that no traces of anthrax or <a href="/wiki/Bubonic_plague" title="Bubonic plague">bubonic plague</a> had been found on human bone fragments discovered during tunnelling.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Invitations to tender for the two principal tunnelling contracts were published in the <a href="/wiki/Official_Journal_of_the_European_Union" title="Official Journal of the European Union">Official Journal of the European Union</a> in August 2009. 'Tunnels West' (C300) was for twin 6.2 kilometres (3.9&#160;mi)-long tunnels from Royal Oak through to the new Crossrail Farringdon Station, with a portal west of Paddington. The 'Tunnels East' (C305) request was for three tunnel sections and 'launch chambers' in east London.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (October 2013)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Contracts were awarded in late 2010: the 'Tunnels West' contract was awarded to <a href="/wiki/BAM_Nuttall" title="BAM Nuttall">BAM Nuttall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ferrovial" title="Ferrovial">Ferrovial</a> Agroman and <a href="/wiki/Kier_Group" title="Kier Group">Kier Construction</a> (BFK); the 'Tunnels East' contract was awarded to <a href="/wiki/Grupo_ACS" class="mw-redirect" title="Grupo ACS">Dragados</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Sisk_%26_Son" class="mw-redirect" title="John Sisk &amp; Son">John Sisk &amp; Son</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The remaining tunnelling contract (C310, Plumstead to North Woolwich), which included a tunnel under the Thames, was awarded to <a href="/wiki/Hochtief" title="Hochtief">Hochtief</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Murphy_(contractor)" title="John Murphy (contractor)">J. Murphy &amp; Sons</a> in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By September 2009, preparatory work for the £1&#160;billion developments at <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Court_Road_tube_station" title="Tottenham Court Road tube station">Tottenham Court Road&#160;station</a> had begun, with buildings (including the <a href="/wiki/London_Astoria" title="London Astoria">Astoria Theatre</a>) being <a href="/wiki/Eminent_domain" title="Eminent domain">compulsorily purchased</a> and demolished.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2010, contracts were awarded to civil engineering companies for the second round of 'enabling work' including 'Royal Oak Portal Taxi Facility Demolition', 'Demolition works for Crossrail Bond Street Station', 'Demolition works for Crossrail Tottenham Court Road Station' and 'Pudding Mill Lane Portal'.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In December 2010, contracts were awarded for most of the tunnelling work.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> To assist with the skills required for the Crossrail project, Crossrail Ltd opened in 2011 the Tunnelling and Underground Construction Academy in Ilford.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> The Academy was handed over to <a href="/wiki/Transport_for_London" title="Transport for London">Transport for London</a> in 2017, who have sub contracted its management to <a href="/wiki/PROCAT" title="PROCAT">PROCAT</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2010, Crossrail was accused of bullying residents whose property lay on the route into selling for less than the market value.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> A subsequent London Assembly report was highly critical of the insensitive way in which Crossrail had dealt with compulsory purchases and the lack of assistance given to the people and businesses affected.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> There were also complaints from music fans, as the <a href="/wiki/London_Astoria" title="London Astoria">London Astoria</a> was forced to close.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ada-panorama-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Ada-panorama-2.jpg/220px-Ada-panorama-2.jpg" width="220" height="54" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Ada-panorama-2.jpg/330px-Ada-panorama-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Ada-panorama-2.jpg/440px-Ada-panorama-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2681" data-file-height="664" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ada-panorama-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The second Tunnel Boring Machine "Ada" en route to the Royal Oak Portal, June 2012</div></div></div>
<p>In December 2011, a contract to ship the excavated material from the tunnel to <a href="/wiki/Wallasea_Island" title="Wallasea Island">Wallasea Island</a><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> was awarded to a joint venture comprising <a href="/wiki/BAM_Nuttall" title="BAM Nuttall">BAM Nuttall</a> Limited and <a href="/wiki/Van_Oord" title="Van Oord">Van Oord</a> UK Limited.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (October 2013)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Between 4.5 and 5 million tonnes of soil will be used to construct a new wetland nature reserve (<a href="/wiki/Wallasea_Wetlands" title="Wallasea Wetlands">Wallasea Wetlands</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC19598532_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC19598532-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The project eventually moved seven million tons of earth.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Boring of the railway tunnels was officially completed at Farringdon on 4 June 2015 in the presence of the Prime Minister and the Mayor of London.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Installation of the track was completed in September 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> The ETCS signalling was scheduled to be tested in the Heathrow tunnels over the winter of 2017/18.<sup id="cite_ref-tflreadinessreport2017_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tflreadinessreport2017-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The south east section of the infrastructure was energised in February 2018, with the first test train run between Plumstead and Abbey Wood that month.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>  In May 2018 the overhead lines were powered up between Westborne Park and Stepney and the installation of platform doors was completed,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> and video was released of the first trains traveling through the tunnels.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>TfL Rail took over Heathrow Connect services from Paddington to Heathrow in May 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The infrastructure will be handed over to TfL in summer 2018, so that they can start trial operations to ensure the reliability of the service.<sup id="cite_ref-tflreadinessreport2017_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tflreadinessreport2017-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tunnel_boring_machines">Tunnel boring machines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tunnel boring machines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The project used eight 7.1-metre (23-foot) diameter <a href="/wiki/Tunnel_boring_machine" title="Tunnel boring machine">tunnel-boring machines</a> (TBM) from <a href="/wiki/Herrenknecht_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Herrenknecht AG">Herrenknecht AG</a> (Germany). Two types are used; 'slurry' type for the Thames tunnel, which involves tunnelling through <a href="/wiki/Chalk" title="Chalk">chalk</a>; and 'Earth Pressure Balance Machines' (EPBM) for tunnelling through clay, sand and gravel (at lower levels through <a href="/wiki/Lambeth_Group" title="Lambeth Group">Lambeth Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thanet_Sands" class="mw-redirect" title="Thanet Sands">Thanet Sands</a> ground formation). The TBMs weigh nearly 1,000&#160;tonnes and are over 100 metres (330 feet) long.<sup id="cite_ref-tbm1_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tbm1-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The TBMs were named (per tradition). Crossrail ran a competition in January 2012 in which over 2500 entries were received and 10 pairs of names short-listed. After a public vote in February 2012, the first three pairs of names were announced on 13 March and the last pair on 16 August 2013:<sup id="cite_ref-TBMnames_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TBMnames-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><i>Ada</i> and <i>Phyllis</i>, Royal Oak to Farringdon section, named after <a href="/wiki/Ada_Lovelace" title="Ada Lovelace">Ada Lovelace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phyllis_Pearsall" title="Phyllis Pearsall">Phyllis Pearsall</a></li>
<li><i>Victoria</i> and <i>Elizabeth</i>, Limmo Peninsula to Farringdon section, named after <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a></li>
<li><i>Mary</i> and <i>Sophia</i>, Plumstead to North Woolwich section, named after the wives of <a href="/wiki/Isambard_Kingdom_Brunel" title="Isambard Kingdom Brunel">Isambard Kingdom Brunel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marc_Isambard_Brunel" title="Marc Isambard Brunel">Marc Isambard Brunel</a></li>
<li><i>Jessica</i> and <i>Ellie</i>, Pudding Mill Lane to Stepney Green and Limmo Peninsula to Victoria Dock sections, named after <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Ennis-Hill" title="Jessica Ennis-Hill">Jessica Ennis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ellie_Simmonds" title="Ellie Simmonds">Ellie Simmonds</a></li></ul>
<h3><span id="Health.2C_safety.2C_and_industrial_relations"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Health,_safety,_and_industrial_relations">Health, safety, and industrial relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Health, safety, and industrial relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Belt-collapse1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Belt-collapse1.JPG/220px-Belt-collapse1.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Belt-collapse1.JPG/330px-Belt-collapse1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Belt-collapse1.JPG/440px-Belt-collapse1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Belt-collapse1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The collapsed gantry (29 September 2012)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Astoria_site_September_2009_CB.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/London_Astoria_site_September_2009_CB.jpg/170px-London_Astoria_site_September_2009_CB.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/London_Astoria_site_September_2009_CB.jpg/255px-London_Astoria_site_September_2009_CB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/London_Astoria_site_September_2009_CB.jpg/340px-London_Astoria_site_September_2009_CB.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Astoria_site_September_2009_CB.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Tottenham Court Road construction site (2009). This included the former site of the <a href="/wiki/London_Astoria" title="London Astoria">London Astoria</a> music venue.</div></div></div>
<p>In 2012 Crossrail faced accusations and evidence of blacklisting. An industrial relations manager Ron Barron, employed by <a href="/wiki/Bechtel" title="Bechtel">Bechtel</a>, had routinely cross-checked job applicants against the <a href="/wiki/Consulting_Association" title="Consulting Association">Consulting Association</a> database.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian-20121201_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-20121201-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> An employment tribunal in 2010 had heard that he introduced the use of the blacklist at his former employer, the construction firm <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bridge_%26_Iron_Company" title="Chicago Bridge &amp; Iron Company">Chicago Bridge &amp; Iron Company</a> (CB&amp;I), and referred to it more than 900 times in 2007 alone. He was found to have unlawfully refused employment to a Philip Willis, with aggravated damages awarded because Barron had added information about Willis to the blacklist.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian-20121201_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-20121201-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2012, a BFK manager challenged their subcontractor, Electrical Installations Services Ltd. (EIS), saying that one of their electricians was a trade union activist. Some days later, Pat Swift, the HR manager for BFK and a regular user of the <a href="/wiki/Consulting_Association" title="Consulting Association">Consulting Association</a>, again challenged EIS. EIS refused to dismiss their worker and lost the contract. Flash pickets were held at the Crossrail site and also at the sites of the BFK partners.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Affairs_Select_Committee" title="Scottish Affairs Select Committee">Scottish Affairs Select Committee</a> called on the UK <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Business,_Innovation_and_Skills" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary of State for Business, Innovation and Skills">Business Secretary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vince_Cable" title="Vince Cable">Vince Cable</a>, to set up a government investigation into blacklisting at Crossrail.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith_and_Chamberlain_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith_and_Chamberlain-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The electrician was reinstated.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Further allegations of blacklisting against Crossrail were made in Parliament in September 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-TCI-06Sep2017_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCI-06Sep2017-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2012, a gantry supporting a spoil hopper at a construction site near <a href="/wiki/Westbourne_Park_tube_station" title="Westbourne Park tube station">Westbourne Park Underground station</a>, used to load rail wagons with excavated waste, collapsed, tipping sideways and causing the adjacent Network Rail line to be closed.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 7 March 2014, Rene Tkacik, a <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakian</a> construction worker, was killed by a piece of falling concrete while working in a tunnel.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> In April 2014, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i> reported details of a leaked internal report, compiled for the Crossrail contractors by an independent safety consultancy. The report was claimed to indicate poor industrial relations over safety issues and that workers were "too scared to report injuries for fear of being sacked".<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Archaeology">Archaeology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Archaeology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The excavation works that took place during the Crossrail project gave archaeologists a unique opportunity to explore the earth underneath London's streets that was previously seen as inaccessible. Crossrail undertook what was described as one of the most extensive archeological programmes ever seen in the UK. Over 100 archaeologists have found tens of thousands of items from 40 sites, spanning 55 million years of London’s history.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Many of the items were placed on show at the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_London_Docklands" title="Museum of London Docklands">Museum of London Docklands</a> from February to September 2017.
Some of the finds include:<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Victims of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Plague_of_London" title="Great Plague of London">Great Plague</a>, a mass grave of 42 skeletons found at <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Street_station" title="Liverpool Street station">Liverpool Street station</a></li>
<li>Thirteen skeletons, thought to be of victims of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a> in the 14th century, uncovered 2.5&#160;m (8&#160;ft 2&#160;in) under the road that surrounds the gardens in <a href="/wiki/Charterhouse_Square" title="Charterhouse Square">Charterhouse Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/Farringdon,_London" title="Farringdon, London">Farringdon</a> in March 2013<sup id="cite_ref-Crossrail_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crossrail-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Matro_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Matro-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Britain" title="Prehistoric Britain">Prehistoric knapped flints</a> discovered in North Woolwich</li>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/Tudor_period" title="Tudor period">Tudor bowling ball</a> found in Stepney Green</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Medieval_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval Britain">Medieval</a> ice skates found near <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Street_station" title="Liverpool Street station">Liverpool Street station</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bison" title="Bison">Bison</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reindeer" title="Reindeer">reindeer</a> bones</li>
<li>Leather shoes dating from the <a href="/wiki/Tudor_period" title="Tudor period">Tudor period</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Roman_currency" title="Roman currency">Roman coins</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">Roman</a> <a href="/wiki/Medallion" class="mw-redirect" title="Medallion">medallion</a> found at Liverpool Street which was issued to mark the New Year celebrations in AD 245. This medallion was only the second ever of its kind to be found in Europe.</li>
<li>Two parts of a <a href="/wiki/Woolly_mammoth" title="Woolly mammoth">woolly mammoth</a> jawbone</li>
<li>The largest piece of <a href="/wiki/Amber" title="Amber">amber</a> ever found in the UK, discovered at Canary Wharf</li>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/Victorian_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="Victorian Britain">Victorian</a> chamber pot found near Stepney Green</li>
<li>13,000 <a href="/wiki/Crosse_%26_Blackwell" title="Crosse &amp; Blackwell">Crosse &amp; Blackwell</a> jars found near Tottenham Court Road from the late 19th and early 20th centuries.</li>
<li>Part of a small barge or fishing vessel from 1223 to 1290 found at <a href="/wiki/Canning_Town" title="Canning Town">Canning Town</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/TfL_Rail" title="TfL Rail">TfL Rail</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Underground_Overground_DLR_Crossrail_map.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/London_Underground_Overground_DLR_Crossrail_map.svg/400px-London_Underground_Overground_DLR_Crossrail_map.svg.png" width="400" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/London_Underground_Overground_DLR_Crossrail_map.svg/600px-London_Underground_Overground_DLR_Crossrail_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/London_Underground_Overground_DLR_Crossrail_map.svg/800px-London_Underground_Overground_DLR_Crossrail_map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1320" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Underground_Overground_DLR_Crossrail_map.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Transport for London services including TfL Rail and Elizabeth line</div></div></div>
<p>Once fully opened, the Elizabeth line will run a familiar London Underground-style all-stops service in the central core section and eastern branches, but initial timetable plans suggest that several trains on the western branches will run semi-fast. Initial proposals suggest <a href="/wiki/Acton_Main_Line_railway_station" title="Acton Main Line railway station">Acton Main Line</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hanwell_railway_station" title="Hanwell railway station">Hanwell</a> will be served only by Heathrow-bound trains.
</p><p>Like the outer sections of <a href="/wiki/Thameslink_(route)" class="mw-redirect" title="Thameslink (route)">Thameslink</a>, the Elizabeth line will share platforms and tracks with other services outside the tunnelled sections. Some run by other train companies will continue to call at various stations on the <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_main_line" title="Great Western main line">Great Western main line</a> branch, and <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Express" title="Heathrow Express">Heathrow Express</a> will continue to run between <a href="/wiki/Paddington_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Paddington railway station">Paddington</a> and Heathrow stations.
</p><p>Approximately half of all Elizabeth line westbound trains, those from Shenfield via Stratford, are expected to terminate at <a href="/wiki/Paddington_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Paddington station">Paddington</a> during peak hours. The eastern section via <a href="/wiki/Stratford_station" title="Stratford station">Stratford</a> is expected to see an additional four trains per hour (tph) during peak times between <a href="/wiki/Gidea_Park_railway_station" title="Gidea Park railway station">Gidea Park</a> and the existing main line <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Street_station" title="Liverpool Street station">Liverpool Street</a> station's high level terminating platforms. Since these trains run over existing above-ground lines from Liverpool Street to <a href="/wiki/Stratford_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Stratford railway station">Stratford</a>, they will not call at <a href="/wiki/Whitechapel_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Whitechapel railway station">Whitechapel</a>.
</p><p>The proposed timetable consists of the following services on the Elizabeth line during peak hours:<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<th class="nowrap unsortable" style="line-height:99%;vertical-align:bottom;padding:.4em .4em .2em;background-position:50% .4em !important;min-width:0.875em;max-width:0.875em;width:0.875em;overflow:hidden"><div style="-webkit-writing-mode: vertical-rl; -o-writing-mode: vertical-rl; -ms-writing-mode: tb-rl;writing-mode: tb-rl; writing-mode: vertical-rl; layout-flow: vertical-ideographic;display: inline-block; -ms-transform: rotate(180deg); -webkit-transform: rotate(180deg); transform: rotate(180deg);;-ms-transform: none ;padding-left:1px;text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Hayes_and_Harlington_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Hayes and Harlington railway station">Hayes and Harlington</a></div>
</th>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Timeline">Timeline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Timeline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Prior to the opening of the main tunnels under central London, it is planned to transfer passenger operations on the outer branches of the Crossrail system to TfL for inclusion in the Crossrail concession. This transfer took place over several stages beginning May 2015. During this initial phase of operation, services are being operated by MTR under the <a href="/wiki/TfL_Rail" title="TfL Rail">TfL Rail</a> brand. Following the practice adopted during the transfer of former <a href="/wiki/Silverlink" title="Silverlink">Silverlink</a> services to London Overground in 2007, TfL will carry out a deep clean of stations and trains on the future Elizabeth line route, install new ticket machines and barriers, introduce <a href="/wiki/Oyster_card" title="Oyster card">Oyster card</a> and <a href="/wiki/Contactless_payment" title="Contactless payment">contactless payment</a>, and ensure all stations are staffed. Existing rolling stock has been rebranded with the TfL Rail identity.<sup id="cite_ref-panel_presentation022015_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-panel_presentation022015-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Services through the central tunnel section are expected to begin in Autumn 2019, although a full east–west service will not begin until a later date due to signalling changes on the Great Western Main Line, and the approximate nine-month delay affecting the Crossrail project.<sup id="cite_ref-boriswatch_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boriswatch-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-London_Reconnections_blog_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-London_Reconnections_blog-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
