<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ticketing">Ticketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Ticketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Ticketing is intended to be integrated with the other London transport systems, and <a href="/wiki/Oyster_card" title="Oyster card">Oyster pay as you go</a> will be accepted. <a href="/wiki/Travelcard" title="Travelcard">Travelcards</a> and concessionary passes will be valid within Greater London. Just as <a href="/wiki/TfL_Rail" title="TfL Rail">TfL Rail</a> current replacement of <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Connect" title="Heathrow Connect">Heathrow Connect</a>, trips to or from Heathrow Airport will be priced at a premium for single fares for the additional cost of using the rail tunnel between Heathrow Airport and <a href="/wiki/Hayes_%26_Harlington_railway_station" title="Hayes &amp; Harlington railway station">Hayes &amp; Harlington</a>, but will be included within travelcards and daily/weekly fare capping as a Zone 6 station.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Crossrail will be integrated with the Underground and National Rail networks, and it is planned to include it on the standard <a href="/wiki/Tube_map" title="Tube map">London Underground Map</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger_numbers">Passenger numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Passenger numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Crossrail has predicted annual passenger numbers of 200 million from its opening in late 2018; this is expected to relieve pressure on London Underground's lines, especially the <a href="/wiki/Central_line_(London_Underground)" title="Central line (London Underground)">Central line</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Farringdon_station" title="Farringdon station">Farringdon</a> is expected to become one of the busiest stations in the UK, due to it being the key interchange station with the North–South <a href="/wiki/Thameslink_(route)" class="mw-redirect" title="Thameslink (route)">Thameslink route</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Once Crossrail is fully open, TfL expects passenger revenue of over £800&#160;million per year in 2020/21 and over £900&#160;million per year from 2022/23.<sup id="cite_ref-tflBP2017-12_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tflBP2017-12-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plans">Plans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Plans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_stations">New stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: New stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Woolwich_Crossrail_station_box_on_Berkeley_Homes_open_day.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Woolwich_Crossrail_station_box_on_Berkeley_Homes_open_day.jpg/220px-Woolwich_Crossrail_station_box_on_Berkeley_Homes_open_day.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Woolwich_Crossrail_station_box_on_Berkeley_Homes_open_day.jpg/330px-Woolwich_Crossrail_station_box_on_Berkeley_Homes_open_day.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Woolwich_Crossrail_station_box_on_Berkeley_Homes_open_day.jpg/440px-Woolwich_Crossrail_station_box_on_Berkeley_Homes_open_day.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="2432" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Woolwich_Crossrail_station_box_on_Berkeley_Homes_open_day.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Woolwich Crossrail station under construction in 2013</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Crossrail_interchange.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Crossrail_interchange.png/220px-Crossrail_interchange.png" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Crossrail_interchange.png/330px-Crossrail_interchange.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Crossrail_interchange.png/440px-Crossrail_interchange.png 2x" data-file-width="910" data-file-height="632" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Crossrail_interchange.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The planned site for the Old Oak Common High Speed 2 / Crossrail interchange</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Woolwich">Woolwich</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Woolwich">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Woolwich_railway_station" title="Woolwich railway station">Woolwich railway station</a></div>
<p>The opening of the new Crossrail station will reduce the journey times from Woolwich, taking 8&#160;minutes to Canary Wharf, 21&#160;m to Bond Street and 47&#160;m to Heathrow.<sup id="cite_ref-railwaytechnologywoolwich_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railwaytechnologywoolwich-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> The construction of a station at Woolwich was not proposed as part of the original Crossrail route. However, the House of Commons Select Committee recognised its inclusion in March 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-railwaytechnologywoolwich_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railwaytechnologywoolwich-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> When Crossrail becomes operational in late 2018, the new station located on the south-east section of the route will see up to 12 trains an hour. It will run during peak hours, connecting south-east London and the Royal Docks with Canary Wharf, central London and beyond.<sup id="cite_ref-railwaytechnologywoolwich_130-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railwaytechnologywoolwich-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Woolwich station is being built on the south-east portion of the Crossrail line that ends at Abbey Wood. The Woolwich redevelopment site at <a href="/wiki/Royal_Arsenal" title="Royal Arsenal">Royal Arsenal</a> is a waterside housing and retail development area adjacent to the Woolwich station. It is spread across approximately 30&#160;ha (74 acres) of land and is being developed by Berkeley Homes.<sup id="cite_ref-railwaytechnologywoolwich_130-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railwaytechnologywoolwich-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> The site is being developed with the construction of approximately 2,517 new homes, in addition to the 1,248 homes already built.<sup id="cite_ref-crossrailwoolwichstation_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crossrailwoolwichstation-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> The area also includes a new heritage quarter along with the Greenwich Heritage Centre and Royal Artillery Museum, as well as infrastructural developments such as retail stores, restaurants and cafés, offices, hotels and a cinema.<sup id="cite_ref-crossrailwoolwichstation_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crossrailwoolwichstation-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_Oak_Common">Old Oak Common</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Old Oak Common">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>As part of the former <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> government's plans for the <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_2" title="High Speed 2">High Speed 2</a> rail link from London to <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, a Crossrail-High Speed 2 interchange would be built at <a href="/wiki/Old_Oak_Common_railway_station" title="Old Oak Common railway station">Old Oak Common</a> (between Paddington and Acton Main Line stations). This would be built as part of High Speed 2 (which would start construction, under Labour's plans, in 2017), so would not be built in the first phase of Crossrail. It would provide interchange to other mainline and TfL lines. The succeeding <a href="/wiki/Cameron%E2%80%93Clegg_coalition" title="Cameron–Clegg coalition">Conservative-Liberal Democrat</a> government adopted that proposal in the plans it put forward for public consultation. This means it is likely to go forward as part of High Speed 2, potentially giving Crossrail an interchange with High Speed 2, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Main_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Western Main Line">Great Western Main Line</a> (GWML), <a href="/wiki/Central_line_(London_Underground)" title="Central line (London Underground)">Central line</a> and London Overground services running through the area.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_proposals">Further proposals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Further proposals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Additional_stations">Additional stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Additional stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:London_City_Airport_DLR_and_Crossrail.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/London_City_Airport_DLR_and_Crossrail.png/220px-London_City_Airport_DLR_and_Crossrail.png" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/London_City_Airport_DLR_and_Crossrail.png/330px-London_City_Airport_DLR_and_Crossrail.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/London_City_Airport_DLR_and_Crossrail.png/440px-London_City_Airport_DLR_and_Crossrail.png 2x" data-file-width="1365" data-file-height="785" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:London_City_Airport_DLR_and_Crossrail.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The route of the Elizabeth line will pass close to the Airport but no station is currently planned</div></div></div>
<h4><span id="Silvertown_.28London_City_Airport.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Silvertown_(London_City_Airport)">Silvertown (London City Airport)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Silvertown (London City Airport)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Although the Crossrail route passes very close to <a href="/wiki/London_City_Airport" title="London City Airport">London City Airport</a>, there not be a station serving the airport directly. London City Airport has proposed the re-opening of <a href="/wiki/Silvertown_railway_station" title="Silvertown railway station">Silvertown railway station</a>, in order to create an interchange between the rail line and the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The self-funded £50m station plan is supported 'in principle' by the <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Newham" title="London Borough of Newham">London Borough of Newham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Provisions for re-opening of the station were made in 2012 by Crossrail.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> However, it is alleged by the airport that <a href="/wiki/Transport_for_London" title="Transport for London">Transport for London</a> is hostile to the idea of a station on the site, a claim disputed by TfL.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, the airport's chief development officer described the lack of a Crossrail station as a "missed opportunity", but did not rule out a future station for the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> The CEO stated in an interview that a station is not essential to the airport's success.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extensions">Extensions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Extensions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Crossrail_extensions.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Crossrail_extensions.png/220px-Crossrail_extensions.png" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Crossrail_extensions.png/330px-Crossrail_extensions.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Crossrail_extensions.png/440px-Crossrail_extensions.png 2x" data-file-width="664" data-file-height="525" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Crossrail_extensions.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Outline map of the possible future Crossrail extensions as recommended in the 2011 RUS<sup id="cite_ref-rus2011_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rus2011-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="To_Reading">To Reading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: To Reading">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>According to the original plans, the western terminus of Crossrail was planned to be Maidenhead. Various commentators advocated an extension of the route further west as far as Reading, especially as it was seen as complementary to the <a href="/wiki/21st_Century_upgrade_of_the_Great_Western_Main_Line#Electrification" class="mw-redirect" title="21st Century upgrade of the Great Western Main Line">Great Western Electrification project</a> which was announced in July 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> A Reading terminus was also recommended by Network Rail's 2011 <a href="/wiki/Route_Utilisation_Strategy" title="Route Utilisation Strategy">Route Utilisation Strategy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rus2011-1_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rus2011-1-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The UK Government and Transport for London evaluated the option of extending to Reading<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> and in March 2014 it was announced that the extension from Maidenhead to Reading would form part of the core Crossrail network from the outset.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Reading_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Reading-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DfT_Reading_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DfT_Reading-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TfL_Reading_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TfL_Reading-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Labour council in Reading supported an extension to Reading<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> but the Conservative MP for Reading East, <a href="/wiki/Rob_Wilson" title="Rob Wilson">Rob Wilson</a>, expressed concerns that Crossrail trains (which will call at every station) will actually be slower than the present Reading-Paddington service. According to Wilson, "We need the right Crossrail, not any Crossrail".<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> However, most existing fast services between Reading and Paddington will remain after the introduction of Crossrail, as there are only paths for the additional two services per hour which the latter will provide.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="To_the_West_Coast_Main_Line">To the West Coast Main Line</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: To the West Coast Main Line">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a>'s July 2011 London &amp; South East <a href="/wiki/Route_Utilisation_Strategy" title="Route Utilisation Strategy">Route Utilisation Strategy</a> (RUS) recommended diverting <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a> (WCML) services from stations between London and <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Central_railway_station" title="Milton Keynes Central railway station">Milton Keynes Central</a> away from <a href="/wiki/Euston_railway_station" title="Euston railway station">Euston</a>, to Crossrail via Old Oak Common, to free up capacity at Euston for <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_2" title="High Speed 2">High Speed 2</a>. This would provide a direct service from the WCML to the <a href="/wiki/Shenfield_railway_station" title="Shenfield railway station">Shenfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canary_Wharf_railway_station" title="Canary Wharf railway station">Canary Wharf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abbey_Wood_railway_station" title="Abbey Wood railway station">Abbey Wood</a>, release London Underground capacity at Euston, make better use of Crossrail's capacity west of Paddington, and improve access to Heathrow Airport from the north.<sup id="cite_ref-rus2011-2_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rus2011-2-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Under this scheme, all Crossrail trains would continue west of Paddington, instead of some of them terminating there. They would serve Heathrow Airport (10 tph), stations to Maidenhead and Reading (6 tph), and stations to Milton Keynes Central (8 tph).<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2014, a statement by transport secretary <a href="/wiki/Patrick_McLoughlin" title="Patrick McLoughlin">Patrick McLoughlin</a> indicated that the government was actively evaluating the extension of Crossrail as far as <a href="/wiki/Tring_railway_station" title="Tring railway station">Tring</a>, with potential Crossrail stops at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Central_station" title="Wembley Central station">Wembley Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harrow_%26_Wealdstone_station" title="Harrow &amp; Wealdstone station">Harrow &amp; Wealdstone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bushey_railway_station" title="Bushey railway station">Bushey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Watford_Junction_railway_station" title="Watford Junction railway station">Watford Junction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kings_Langley_railway_station" title="Kings Langley railway station">Kings Langley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apsley_railway_station" title="Apsley railway station">Apsley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hemel_Hempstead_railway_station" title="Hemel Hempstead railway station">Hemel Hempstead</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berkhamsted_railway_station" title="Berkhamsted railway station">Berkhamsted</a>. The extension would relieve some pressure from London Underground and London Euston station while also increasing connectivity. Conditions to the extension are that any extra services would not affect the planned service pattern for confirmed routes, as well as affordability.<sup id="cite_ref-Crossrail_Tring_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crossrail_Tring-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian-crossrail-0814_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-crossrail-0814-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> This proposal was shelved in August 2016 due to "poor overall value for money to the taxpayer".<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="To_Gravesend_and_Hoo_Junction">To Gravesend and Hoo Junction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: To Gravesend and Hoo Junction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The route to <a href="/wiki/Gravesend,_Kent" class="mw-redirect" title="Gravesend, Kent">Gravesend</a> has been safeguarded by the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a>, although it was made clear that as at February 2008 there was no plan to extend Crossrail beyond the then-current scheme.<sup id="cite_ref-safeguarding_update_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-safeguarding_update-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
The following stations are on the protected route extension to Gravesend: <a href="/wiki/Belvedere_railway_station" title="Belvedere railway station">Belvedere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erith_railway_station" title="Erith railway station">Erith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slade_Green_railway_station" title="Slade Green railway station">Slade Green</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dartford_railway_station" title="Dartford railway station">Dartford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stone_Crossing_railway_station" title="Stone Crossing railway station">Stone Crossing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenhithe_railway_station" title="Greenhithe railway station">Greenhithe</a> for <a href="/wiki/Bluewater_(shopping_centre)" title="Bluewater (shopping centre)">Bluewater</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swanscombe_railway_station" title="Swanscombe railway station">Swanscombe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northfleet_railway_station" title="Northfleet railway station">Northfleet</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gravesend_railway_station" title="Gravesend railway station">Gravesend</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
In January 2018 it was revealed that the Mayor of London, <a href="/wiki/Sadiq_Khan" title="Sadiq Khan">Sadiq Khan</a>, had included an extension of Crossrail to <a href="/wiki/Ebbsfleet_International_railway_station" title="Ebbsfleet International railway station">Ebbsfleet</a> as part of a transport plan between 2021 and 2041. TfL stated that they were considering an extension to Ebbsfleet.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Heathrow_Express">Heathrow Express</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Heathrow Express">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The RUS also proposes integrating Heathrow Express services from Heathrow Terminal 5 into Crossrail to relieve the GWML and reduce the need for passengers to change at Paddington.<sup id="cite_ref-rus2011-3_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rus2011-3-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_lines">New lines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: New lines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="Crossrail_2_.28Chelsea.E2.80.93Hackney.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Crossrail_2_(Chelsea–Hackney)">Crossrail 2 (Chelsea–Hackney)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Crossrail 2 (Chelsea–Hackney)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Crossrail_2" title="Crossrail 2">Crossrail 2</a></div>
<p>Crossrail 2 is a proposed rail route in South East England, running from nine stations in Surrey to three in Hertfordshire providing a new rail link across London on the Crossrail network. It would connect the South Western Main Line to the West Anglia Main Line, via Victoria and Kings Cross St Pancras, intended to alleviate severe overcrowding that would otherwise occur on commuter rail routes into Central London by the 2030s. It would interchange with Crossrail 1 at Tottenham Court Road, the only interchange between the two lines.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Management_and_franchise">Management and franchise</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Management and franchise">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Funding for the project came from:
</p>
<ul><li>Transport for London</li>
<li>Mayoral <a href="/wiki/Community_Infrastructure_Levy" class="mw-redirect" title="Community Infrastructure Levy">Community Infrastructure Levy</a> (a local tax charged on property developments across Greater London, with different charging rates for each London borough)<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Crossrail Business Rate Supplement (additional business rates)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Town_and_Country_Planning_Act_1990#Part_III,_Control_Over_Development" title="Town and Country Planning Act 1990">Section 106 Agreement</a> payments</li>
<li>Over-site development opportunities</li>
<li>UK Government</li>
<li>City of London Corporation</li>
<li>Major landowners Canary Wharf Group, Heathrow Airport Holdings, and Berkeley Homes.</li></ul>
<p>Crossrail is being built by Crossrail Ltd, jointly owned by <a href="/wiki/Transport_for_London" title="Transport for London">Transport for London</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a> until December 2008, when full ownership was transferred to TfL. Crossrail has a £15.9&#160;billion funding package in place<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> for the construction of the line. Although the branch lines to the west and to Shenfield will still be owned by Network Rail, the tunnel will be owned and operated by TfL.<sup id="cite_ref-GA_inv_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GA_inv-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 18 July 2014, TfL <a href="/wiki/London_Rail" title="London Rail">London Rail</a> said that MTR Corp had won the concession to operate the services for eight years, with an option for two more years.<sup id="cite_ref-rg20140718_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rg20140718-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The concession will be similar to London Overground.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (October 2013)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> It is planned for <a href="/wiki/Rail_franchising_in_Great_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="Rail franchising in Great Britain">the franchise</a> to run for eight years from May 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-rg20140718_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rg20140718-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> taking over control of Shenfield metro services from <a href="/wiki/Abellio_Greater_Anglia" class="mw-redirect" title="Abellio Greater Anglia">Abellio Greater Anglia</a> in May 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-rg20140718_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rg20140718-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> and Reading / Heathrow services from <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Railway_(train_operating_company)" title="Great Western Railway (train operating company)">Great Western Railway</a> in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-London_Reconnections_blog_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-London_Reconnections_blog-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In anticipation of an May 2015 transfer of Shenfield to Liverpool Street services from the Greater Anglia franchise to Crossrail, the invitation to tender for the 2012–2013 franchise required the new rail operator to set up a separate "Crossrail Business Unit" for those services before the end of 2012. This unit was to allow transfer of services to the new Crossrail Train Operating Concession (CTOC) operator during the next franchise.<sup id="cite_ref-GA_inv_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GA_inv-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_341_and_342" class="mw-redirect" title="British Rail Class 341 and 342">British Rail Class 341 and 342</a>, proposed rolling stock for an earlier unbuilt Crossrail scheme</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Center_City_Commuter_Connection" title="Center City Commuter Connection">Center City Commuter Connection</a> – a similar project in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, Pennsylvania; opened in 1984</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Crossrail_2" title="Crossrail 2">Crossrail 2</a> - Second proposed Crossrail route, running north east to south west.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Great_Eastern_Main_Line" title="Great Eastern Main Line">Great Eastern Main Line</a> - Eastern branch of Crossrail</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Main_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Western Main Line">Great Western Main Line</a> - Western section of Crossrail</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport_transport_proposals" title="Heathrow Airport transport proposals">Heathrow Airport transport proposals</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/North%E2%80%93South_Rail_Link" title="North–South Rail Link">North–South Rail Link</a> – a similar project in <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>, Massachusetts; not yet started</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oslo_Tunnel" title="Oslo Tunnel">Oslo Tunnel</a> – a similar project in <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a>, Norway; opened in 1980</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Picc-Vic_tunnel" title="Picc-Vic tunnel">Picc-Vic tunnel</a> – a similar project in <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>; never built</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Rail transport in the United Kingdom">Rail transport in the United Kingdom</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9seau_Express_R%C3%A9gional" title="Réseau Express Régional">Réseau Express Régional</a> (RER) – the similar cross-city rail network in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thameslink_Programme" title="Thameslink Programme">Thameslink Programme</a>, upgrading of existing <a href="/wiki/Thameslink" title="Thameslink">north–south line</a> through Central London</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thames_Tideway_Scheme" title="Thames Tideway Scheme">Thames Tideway Tunnel</a> - sewage tunnel being built in London at the same time as Crossrail using similar methods</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crossrail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
